The ordered chiral homology satisfies
a factorisation constraint at this boundary stratum of
$\overline{\cM}_2$:
\[
  \int_{\Sigma_2}^{\mathrm{ord}} Y_\hbar
  \;\xrightarrow{\;\mathrm{res}\;}\;
  \int_{E_\tau}^{\mathrm{ord}} Y_\hbar
  \;\otimes\;
  \int_{E_{\tau'}}^{\mathrm{ord}} Y_\hbar.
\]
In the non-separating degeneration $\Sigma_2 \to E_\tau$
(a single cycle pinches, reducing the genus by one),
the period matrix
$\Omega = \bigl(\begin{smallmatrix}
\tau & \epsilon \\ \epsilon & i/\epsilon
\end{smallmatrix}\bigr)$
degenerates as $\epsilon \to 0$, and the genus-$2$ theory
reduces to the genus-$1$ theory of
\S\ref{sec:elliptic-ordered} with additional data from
the pinched cycle.
This non-separating degeneration carries genuinely
genus-$2$ information (the off-diagonal entry
$\Omega_{12}$); the separating degeneration does not.
\end{remark}


% ================================================================
% MOVED FROM between ``Examples'' and ``Chiral quantum groups''; now after elliptic curves
\section{Comparison with related work}
\label{sec:comparison}

Two existing programmes address the integration of braided
algebraic structures over surfaces:
Ben-Zvi--Brochier--Jordan integrate braided monoidal
\emph{categories}, while Latyntsev constructs chiral
homology for factorisation \emph{coalgebras}. Ordered chiral
homology occupies a different position: it integrates chiral
\emph{algebras} at the chain level, applies uniformly to all
four shadow classes, and does not require a finite ribbon
category.

\begin{conjecture}[BBJ decategorification]
\label{conj:bbj-decategorification}
Let $\fg$ be a finite-dimensional simple Lie algebra,
$k$ an admissible rational level (so that
$\mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$ is a finite ribbon category with
$q = e^{2\pi i/(k + h^\vee)}$), $\Sigma$ a closed oriented
surface, and $X$ a smooth projective curve of the same genus.
\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}]
  \textup{(Decategorification quasi-isomorphism.)}
  There is a quasi-isomorphism
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:bbj-comparison-standalone}
    \HH_*\Bigl(\int_\Sigma \mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)\Bigr)
    \;\simeq\;
    \int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} V_k(\fg),
  \end{equation}
  where the left side is the Hochschild homology of the
  BBJ categorical factorisation homology and the right
  side is the ordered chiral homology of the affine
  vertex algebra.
\item[\textup{(ii)}]
  \textup{($\Ethree$-intertwining.)}
  The quasi-isomorphism~\eqref{eq:bbj-comparison-standalone}
  intertwines the $\Ethree$-structure on the derived
  chiral centre
  $Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\fg))$ with the
  $\Ethree$-structure on the Hochschild cochains of the
  categorical invariant.
\item[\textup{(iii)}]
  \textup{(Scope: admissible rational levels.)}
  The comparison requires $k$ admissible rational, so that
  $\mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$ is a finite ribbon category
  (the BBJ construction uses the ribbon structure and
  the finiteness condition). At irrational or generic $k$,
  the categorical side is not defined; ordered chiral
  homology applies without restriction.
\item[\textup{(iv)}]
  \textup{(Kernel.)}
  The kernel of the decategorification
  map~\eqref{eq:bbj-comparison-standalone} detects higher
  categorical data: objects of
  $\int_\Sigma \mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$ that are invisible
  at the chain level (i.e.\ whose Hochschild homology
  vanishes).
\end{enumerate}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Ben-Zvi--Brochier--Jordan]
\label{rem:bbj}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:bbj-decategorification} makes precise
the expected relationship between Ben-Zvi, Brochier, and
Jordan's factorisation homology for braided monoidal
categories~\cite{BBJ15,BBJ16} and ordered chiral homology.
The two constructions operate at different levels:
\begin{itemize}
\item BBJ integrate braided monoidal \emph{categories}
  over surfaces (categorical level).
\item Ordered chiral homology integrates chiral
  \emph{algebras} over curves (chain level).
\end{itemize}
For affine Kac--Moody at admissible rational level:
BBJ's $\int_\Sigma \mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$ is a category,
while $\int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} V_k(\fg)$ is a chain complex.
Part~(i) of the conjecture asserts that Hochschild homology
of the former recovers the latter.

For class $M$ (Virasoro at generic $c$): the BBJ
framework requires a finite ribbon category, which is
not available for generic central charge. Ordered chiral
homology applies without restriction to class $M$,
providing an integration theory where the categorical
approach does not (currently) reach.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Latyntsev]
\label{rem:latyntsev}
Latyntsev~\cite{Latyntsev23} constructs chiral homology
for factorisation coalgebras on curves, providing an
algebraic counterpart to the analytic construction of
this paper. The relationship between the two approaches
at the chain level, particularly for irregular
singularities (class $M$), deserves further investigation.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Wilson lines by ambient dimension]
\label{rem:wilson-line-classification}
The type of Wilson line, the form of the $R$-matrix, and
the resulting Yang--Baxter equation are controlled by the
ambient space dimension. The following table summarizes the
principal cases.

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\small
\begin{tabular}{@{} l l l l l @{}}
\toprule
Ambient & $R$-matrix & YBE & Algebra & Integrable system \\
\midrule
$\RR^3$ & constant $R$ & quantum $R_{12}R_{13}R_{23} = R_{23}R_{13}R_{12}$
  & $U_q(\fg)$ & Jones polynomial \\
$\RR \times \CC$ & $r(z)$, $1$ spectral & CYBE $[r_{12},r_{13}] + \mathrm{cyc} = 0$
  & $Y_\hbar(\fg)$ & Gaudin \\
$\RR^2 \times \CC$ & $R(u)$, spectral & quantum spectral YBE
  & $U_q(L\fg)$ & XXZ \\
$\CC^2$ & $r(z,w)$, $2$ params & $2$d CYBE
  & $\fg[u,v]$ & Hitchin on surface \\
$\RR \times \CC^2$ & $R(u,v)$, $2$ spectral & quantum + dynamical
  & $U_{q,t}(\widehat{\widehat{\fg}})$ & eCM + Hitchin \\
$\CC^3$ (CY) & $r + \ZZ \times \ZZ$ grading & $6$d YBE
  & $\Eone$-chiral QG & DT/BPS \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\noindent
This paper works in the $\RR \times \CC$ setting
(Costello's $4$d Chern--Simons~\cite{CWY1,CWY2,CFG26,CG17}),
producing the Yangian $Y_\hbar(\fg)$ as the
line-operator algebra.
The extensions to $\RR^2 \times \CC$ (quantum loop
algebras), $\CC^2$ (double current algebras),
$\RR \times \CC^2$ (quantum toroidal algebras), and
$\CC^3$ ($6$d holomorphic Chern--Simons defects) are
frontier directions; ordered chiral homology provides
the natural integration theory for the
$\RR \times \CC$ column.
\end{remark}


% ================================================================
\section{Further results}
\label{sec:further-results}

Three results from the monograph~\cite{Lorgat26I} that
complement the constructions of this paper.

\begin{theorem}[Verlinde polynomial family; {\cite[Thm.~\ref*{thm:verlinde-polynomial-family}]{Lorgat26I}}]
\label{thm:verlinde-poly-standalone}
The Verlinde dimension $Z_g(k) = \sum_{j=0}^k S_{0j}^{2-2g}$
for $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2$ at level $k$ is a polynomial
$P_g(n)$ of degree $3(g-1)$ in $n = k + 2$ with
$P_g(n) = n^{g-1}(n^2 - 1) \cdot R_{g-2}(n^2)$.
Through $g = 6$: $P_2 = n(n^2{-}1)/6$,
$P_3 = n^2(n^2{-}1)(n^2{+}11)/180$,
$P_4 = n^3(n^2{-}1)(2n^4{+}23n^2{+}191)/7560$.
Leading coefficient: $\zeta(2g{-}2)/(2^{g-2}\pi^{2g-2})$.
Rational generating function:
$G_n(x) = \sum_{j=1}^{n-1} 1/(1 - a_j x)$,
$a_j = n/(2\sin^2(\pi j/n))$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proposition}[Critical level: monodromy trivialises; {\cite[Prop.~\ref*{prop:critical-level-ordered}]{Lorgat26I}}]
\label{prop:critical-standalone}
At $k = -h^\vee$ for $V_{-2}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$:
$\kappa = 0$, ALL monodromy is trivial
\textup{(}eigenvalues $-1, +3$ are integers\textup{)},
$\dim H^1$ doubles from $4$ to $8$,
Koszulness fails, and the bar cohomology spreads to
$\Omega^*(\operatorname{Op}_{\mathfrak{sl}_2}(D))$.
The spectral sequence mechanism:
$d_k = d_{\mathrm{crit}} + (k+2)\,\delta$; at
$\lambda = k + 2 = 0$, the $d_1$ page vanishes.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proposition}[Genus-$2$ conformal blocks by degree; {\cite[Prop.~\ref*{prop:g2-conformal-block-degree}]{Lorgat26I}}]
\label{prop:g2-cb-standalone}
At integer level $k$, the degree-$2$ conformal block count
on $\Sigma_2$ is
$\mathrm{CB}_{2,2}(k) = 2k(k+1)(k+2)/3$
\textup{(}cubic in $k$\textup{)}. At $k = 1$: $4$
\textup{(}triplet truncated\textup{)}.
At $k = 2$: $16$. At $k = 3$: $40$.
\end{proposition}


% ================================================================
\section{Conclusion and open problems}
\label{sec:conclusion}

This paper defines ordered chiral homology
$\int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} \cA$ for $\Eone$-chiral algebras
on algebraic curves, constructs the chiral
$\Ethree$-algebra
$\CE^{\mathrm{ch}}_k(\fg)$ as the holomorphic
refinement of the Costello--Francis--Gwilliam perturbative
Chern--Simons algebra, and establishes the chiral quantum
group equivalence (Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-qg-equiv})
relating vertex $R$-matrices, $\Ainf$-structures, and
chiral coproducts as three faces of a single ordered bar
complex.
The chiral Yangian datum
(Definition~\ref{def:chiral-yangian-datum}) packages
this equivalence as a single axiomatised object,
and Conjecture~\ref{conj:yangian-ordered-center} predicts
the full structure of the ordered derived chiral centre:
infinite-dimensional, carrying an $\Etwo$-algebra
structure via the classical Deligne conjecture, and
recovering $\fg$ from the degree-$1$ Gerstenhaber bracket.
The representation-theoretic kernel formula
$\dim\ker(\av_n) = d^n - \binom{n+d-1}{d-1}$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:ker-av-schur-weyl}) provides the
quantitative underpinning: the ordered data grows
exponentially while the symmetric shadow grows polynomially.
Five explicit computations across the shadow
classification (Heisenberg: class~$G$; affine Kac--Moody:
class~$L$; $\beta\gamma$: class~$C$; Virasoro:
class~$M$; Yangian: genuinely $\Eone$) verify the
formality bridge, the regular/irregular dichotomy,
and the Stokes phenomena that distinguish gauge theory
from gravity at the level of the KZ $\cD$-module.
Section~\ref{sec:elliptic-ordered} extends the construction
to genus~$1$, computing
$\int_{E_\tau}^{\mathrm{ord}} Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
degree by degree: the Belavin elliptic $r$-matrix replaces
the rational $r$-matrix, the KZB connection replaces the
KZ connection, and the $B$-cycle monodromy produces the
quantum group parameter $q = e^{2\pi i \hbar}$.
Section~\ref{sec:genus2-ordered} extends to genus~$2$,
where the $2 \times 2$ Siegel period matrix, the prime
form, and the genus-$2$ surface braid group produce a
theory with non-vanishing Euler characteristics at every
degree ($\chi = -12$ at degree~$2$, compared with $-4$ at
genus~$1$).

The following problems remain open.

\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]

\item \textup{(The $\Ethree$ identification
for affine Kac--Moody: resolved.)}
Theorem~\ref{thm:e3-identification} proves that the
derived chiral centre
$Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(V_k(\fg))$ and the
CFG algebra $\cA^\lambda$ are isomorphic as formal
deformation families of $\Ethree$-algebras over
$(k+h^\vee) H^3(\fg)[[k+h^\vee]]$, for simple~$\fg$.
The proof is obstruction-theoretic: the
one-dimensionality of $H^3(\fg)$ for simple~$\fg$
forces the two deformations to agree at each order in
$(k+h^\vee)$, given the matching of associated graded
algebras and $\Pthree$ brackets on the formal disk
(Theorem~\ref{thm:chiral-e3-cfg}).
The remaining question is the extension to
non-simple~$\fg$, where $H^3(\fg)$ may be
higher-dimensional and the order-by-order uniqueness
argument requires additional invariants to pin down the
deformation class.

\item \textup{(The ordered derived chiral centre of the
chiral Yangian.)}
Conjecture~\ref{conj:yangian-ordered-center} predicts
that the ordered derived chiral centre of
$Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)^{\mathrm{ch}}$ is
infinite-dimensional and carries an $\Etwo$-algebra
structure (but not $\Ethree$, since the symmetric bar does
not exist for genuinely $\Eone$-chiral algebras).
Proposition~\ref{prop:ker-av-schur-weyl} proves the
representation-theoretic kernel formula
$\dim\ker(\av_n) = d^n - \binom{n+d-1}{d-1}$ for any
$d$-dimensional representation of any simple Lie algebra;
the open content is the passage from
this bound to the actual cohomology of the ordered bar
complex at each degree. In particular: does the degree-$1$
Gerstenhaber bracket on the ordered chiral centre
recover $\fg$ for all simple Lie algebras, or is the
identification specific to $\mathfrak{sl}_2$?

\item \textup{(Holomorphic Chern--Simons invariants of
curves.)}
The chiral $\Ethree$-algebra
$\CE^{\mathrm{ch}}_k(\fg)$ on a smooth proper
curve~$X$ of genus~$g$ should produce, via the
higher-genus ordered chiral homology and factorisation on
$\overline{\cM}_{g,n}$, invariants of $(X, \fg, k)$
that refine Reshetikhin--Turaev invariants in the same
way that perturbative Chern--Simons refines Witten's
partition function.
Concretely: does the genus-$g$ ordered chiral homology
$\int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} \CE^{\mathrm{ch}}_k(\fg)$
recover the perturbative Chern--Simons partition function
$Z_{\mathrm{CS}}(X, \fg, k)$ as its $\Sigma_n$-coinvariant
shadow, and what invariants live in the kernel of
the averaging map $\av$?

\item \textup{(The $\cW_{1+\infty}$ chiral quantum group:
remaining questions.)}
Theorem~\ref{thm:w-infty-chiral-qg} establishes that
$\cW_{1+\infty}[\Psi]$ carries a chiral quantum group
datum with OPE compatibility at all spins, proved by
the coderivation property on the Koszul-locus bar complex
and independently by the JKL vertex bialgebra theorem on
the CoHA. A constant coproduct does not exist for
$c \neq 0$ (conformal anomaly obstruction).
Theorem~\ref{thm:glN-chiral-qg} extends this to
$\cW_N$ at all finite $N \geq 2$, where the $R$-matrix
is Yang's matrix $R(u) = u\, I + \Psi\, P$ and the RTT
is non-trivial.
The vertex-algebraic antipode question
(Remark~\ref{rem:w-infty-vertex-gap}) is resolved:
Proposition~\ref{prop:w-infty-antipode-obstruction} and
Remark~\ref{rem:antipode-ope-analysis} show that
$S(T(u)) = T(u)^{-1}$ does \emph{not} lift to a vertex
Hopf algebra structure; $S$ preserves the Heisenberg OPE
but fails on the Virasoro OPE (quartic pole shift
$2(\Psi-1)(\Psi-2)$), and the spectral Hopf axiom fails
independently.
The remaining open question is the Stokes
multipliers of the irregular KZ connection for $\cW_N$
(Poincar\'e rank $N-1$), and whether they encode the
higher-spin BPS spectrum.

\item \textup{(Higher-genus ordered chiral homology.)}
Section~\ref{sec:ord-ch-hom} defines ordered chiral
homology at genus~$0$,
Section~\ref{sec:elliptic-ordered} constructs the
genus-$1$ theory
$\int_{E_\tau}^{\mathrm{ord}} Y_\hbar(\mathfrak{sl}_2)$
explicitly, and Section~\ref{sec:genus2-ordered} extends the
construction to genus~$2$, where the period matrix is a
$2 \times 2$ symmetric matrix, the KZB connection acquires
three modular components, and the Euler characteristic
$\chi = -12$ at degree~$2$ is three times the genus-$1$
value. At genus $g \geq 3$, the curvature
obstruction $d^2_{\mathrm{fib}} = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \omega_g$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT), where $\omega_g = c_1(\lambda)$ is
the Hodge class on $\overline{\cM}_g$, requires a
period-corrected differential whose coefficients involve
the $(g \times g)$-matrix $(\mathrm{Im}\, \Omega)^{-1}$
of the Siegel period matrix.
Does the ordered chiral chain complex at genus~$g \geq 3$
define a flat connection over $\overline{\cM}_g$
compatible with the Mumford--Morita class $\kappa_1$,
and does the resulting system of conformal blocks satisfy
factorisation at the boundary divisors of
$\overline{\cM}_g$?

\item \textup{(Trigonometric and elliptic $R$-matrices
beyond $\mathfrak{sl}_2$.)}
Section~\ref{sec:elliptic-ordered} treats the Belavin
elliptic $R$-matrix for $\mathfrak{sl}_2$ on $E_\tau$.
The trigonometric $R$-matrix
$R^{\mathrm{trig}}(u)$ (quantum affine
algebras) and the elliptic Belavin $R$-matrix for
$\mathfrak{sl}_N$ ($N \geq 3$) produce richer ordered
chiral homology with qualitatively different behaviour:
higher-order Stokes phenomena, theta-function monodromy,
and flat sections valued in elliptic hypergeometric
integrals.
Does the regular/irregular dichotomy of
Theorem~\ref{thm:main-ord-ch} extend to a trichotomy
(regular, irregular-rational, irregular-elliptic)
correlated with the three types of quantum groups?
For $\mathfrak{sl}_N$, what is the degree-$2$ de~Rham
cohomology of the KZB local system of rank $N^2$ on
$E_\tau \setminus \{0\}$, and how does the isospin
decomposition into irreducibles of
$V^{\otimes 2} = \operatorname{Sym}^2 V \oplus
\bigwedge^2 V$ generalise?

\item \textup{(Categorification.)}
Ben-Zvi--Brochier--Jordan~\cite{BBJ15,BBJ16} integrate
braided monoidal categories over surfaces; ordered chiral
homology integrates chiral algebras over curves.
Conjecture~\ref{conj:bbj-decategorification} makes
the expected bridge precise: the decategorification
quasi-isomorphism~\eqref{eq:bbj-comparison-standalone}
identifies the Hochschild homology of the categorical
invariant $\int_\Sigma \mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$ with the
ordered chiral homology
$\int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} V_k(\fg)$.
Is there a direct functor realising this comparison
that intertwines the $\Ethree$-structures (part~(ii)),
and what is the structure of the kernel (part~(iv)):
which objects of $\int_\Sigma \mathrm{Rep}_q(\fg)$
are invisible at the chain level?

\item \textup{(Refinements of the topological enhancement.)}
Khan--Zeng~\cite{KhanZeng25} prove the topological
enhancement at the classical (PVA) level;
Proposition~\ref{prop:khan-zeng-topological} extends
this to the full quantum vertex algebra $V_k(\fg)$
at non-critical level, using the exactness of the
Sugawara element in $V_k(\fg)$.
Two refinements remain open: (a)~does the topological
$\Ethree$-structure on
$\CE^{\mathrm{ch}}_k(\fg)$ extend to a
topological $\Ethree$-structure on the higher-genus
ordered chiral homology
$\int_X^{\mathrm{ord}} \CE^{\mathrm{ch}}_k(\fg)$
for $g \geq 2$, and (b)~at the critical level
$k = -h^\vee$, where the Sugawara element is undefined,
is the resulting holomorphic $\Ethree$-algebra
distinguished from the topological one by a computable
invariant (a secondary characteristic class of the
chiral $\Ethree$-algebra)?

\end{enumerate}
